    <li> [Pros] Only 1 Attachment for 19 adjustable settings (!!!), waterproof (!!!), ergonomic, powerful enough to not require too many swipes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;[Cons] None that I&#x27;ve found. Maybe other color options for the rubber would be nice?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is the perfect beard trimmer, especially at this price range (was purchased holiday season 2014 for $35). I understand that some people might give a bad review because they got a defective product; sometimes that just happens. That&#x27;s one reason we shop Amazon, it&#x27;s no hassle to get a replacement. -- But 95% of these complaints I&#x27;m seeing really aren&#x27;t legitimate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Allow me to note the strengths of this trimmer, before debunking some of the cons:&lt;br /&gt;~ The 19 Setting Single Attachment: Anyone who really maintains facial hair understands how crucial fine length-settings are. 1 millimeter&#x27;s difference in length of hair on a face is noticeable. There&#x27;s plenty of horrible trimmers out there with a couple of set attachments; with this one you can adjust in 0.5mm increments with JUST ONE attachment to keep up with (and clean!!!)&lt;br /&gt;~ Waterproof: ... ... It&#x27;s waterproof. Want to use it in the shower? It&#x27;s waterproof. Want to clean the head? It&#x27;s waterproof. Beard trimmings sticking to the rubber handle and can&#x27;t be brushed off (an old pet-peeve of mine). IT&#x27;S WATERPROOF.&lt;br /&gt;~ Ergonomics and Power: Pretty simple on this; it fits the hand nicely, the head isn&#x27;t overly large so you can pop off the attachment and do detail work, and the motor provides ample power to clip hair cleanly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now to address the common criticisms, which don&#x27;t make a lot of sense to me honestly:&lt;br /&gt;~ &amp;#34;I have to oil it after every use! Wah wah!&amp;#34;: Um... use some common sense here. The instructions do say to oil it after every use, but... come on guys. Really? It&#x27;s able to be used WET. If you&#x27;re constantly running it through water, would you need to reapply oil more? Sure. Too much work for you? Use it as a dry razor and oil it as you normally would. -- You do not have to oil this any more than any other trimmer, unless of course you are washing away the oil all the time.&lt;br /&gt;~ &amp;#34;Battery no last me long, only 50 minutes. Wah wah!&amp;#34;: ... Ok, I&#x27;m noticing a trend here. Apparently, technology should run on fairy dust and magical rainbow farts or something. Who out there is seriously using their beard trimmer for 50 minutes in one use??? Or even a week??? So... let me get this straight: It&#x27;s too much to ask that this hand-held, waterproof, compact beard-cutting machine be charged for a day once a week. ... ... ... ... Ok Justin Beiber, let&#x27;s go to Spoiled Prince Land.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I could go on with some of the other comments I&#x27;ve seen about parts snapping off or something -- Again, I&#x27;m not saying there has never been a defective product shipped, but I will say this thing is really heavy and sturdy and well... people who complain about having to reapply oil after WASHING IT OFF probably also have clumsy hands and don&#x27;t pay attention to the way they are supposed to push/pull something and just break it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Conclusion: Best beard trimmer 35 bucks could buy. This should be a 4.5+ Star rated device.as you normally would. -- You do not have to oil this any more than any other trimmer, unless of course you are washing away the oil all the time.&lt;br /&gt;~ &amp;#34;Battery no last me long, only 50 minutes. Pretty sure I&#x27;m going to lose that little brush in a week - assuming I didn&#x27;t already lose it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, it comes with a little bottle of oil and according to the instructions, it says you are supposed to oil it before AND after EVERY use. That seems a little ridiculous to me. Not only that, but from the image shown in the instructions, it looks like you have to oil the INSIDE of the shaver head which would mean you&#x27;d have to remove two screws to gain access to the inside of the head. They have lost their minds if they think I&#x27;m going to take something apart TWICE every time I use it to oil it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m hoping it&#x27;s a typo in the instructions where it says you&#x27;re supposed to do this before and after every use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Oh, one other very minor thing  - you can not use this while charging. Since there&#x27;s nothing to actually plug into the shaver, you have to leave it in the charging cradle for it to charge. Which means if the battery goes dead and you want to use it really quickly, you have to wait for it to charge up a bit before you can use it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Since this is made to work wet or dry though, I&#x27;m not really surprised that it can&#x27;t be plugged in since I doubt they want someone doing something foolish like stepping into the shower holding something plugged into an outlet :)</li>

    <li> bought this after my Philips QT4050 broke from fall down a flight of stairs.  I found this on sale at Future Shop and decided to get this over the another 4050.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would rate this 2.5 out of 5, but Amazon doesn&#x27;t allow that, and I think it is closure to a 3 then a 2.  For every positive this razor has a negative.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as the charging stand goes, if you are someone that likes to keep things on top of your counter this is possibly the nicest looking trimmer and stand on the market.  I personally don&#x27;t, after it&#x27;s finished charging I place it in the drawer, but if looks are important, this trimmer gets a 5 in the department.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The charging stand does have a negative.  The light on the stand only indicates that charger is actually on the stand correctly.  The light on the stand will either be on, meaning the trimmer is on the stand, or the light will be off.  The light is only red, it will not change colors when it is done charging, nor will it turn off.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;When fully charged this has an incredible battery life, however the trimmer does not have any indicator to let you know when the battery is dying or how much life you have left.  This is a huge negative, since this trimmer can only be used as a cordless.  There is no option to use a cord, the trimmer can only be charged by sitting on the stand.  If the trimmer starts to die before you are finished, you are out of luck.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The motor on this is very quite.  It is easily the quickest one I&#x27;ve every owned.  However, that benefit is probably achieved by under powering the motor.  I found the 4050 to have a little more power, which means the 4070 which is also cheaper then this, may have a lot more power then this.  I found myself having to do some extra passes with this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The biggest benefit of this trimmer is probably the fact that you can use it in the shower, and clean it by running water through it.  The draw back is the maintenance that is required because ofthis.  In a time when more and more trimmers are becoming Maintenance-free, this trimmer requires you to oil it&#x27;s blades both before and after each use.  With that said, I still find it faster to wash this under water and apply 3 drops of oil, then have to clean the trimmer with a brush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I actually like the comb, it feels fine against my face and doesn&#x27;t scratch.  However taking it off does feel odd sometimes, and sometimes it does feel like you have to force it off and it might break.  With that said the trimmer does feel like it is solidly made, so maybe it&#x27;s something I&#x27;ll get us to.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for the price.  I do think this is overpriced.  I live in Toronto, Canada.  At Future Shop this was priced regularly at $69, the Philips 4050 was at $49 and the 4070 at 64.  I got it on sale for 59.  I would not buy this for regular price, and honestly if I had to replace it, I wouldn&#x27;t spend $59 on again either.  This shouldn&#x27;t be price more then Philips 4050 at $49.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In the end, like I mentioned at the top, this is a decent trimmer, but is nothing to write home about, and it is very overpriced.  It has some nice benefits, but also some huge negatives.  It does the job, but there are trimmer that do just as good of a job at a lot cheaper price.</li>

The ER224S always gave you an uneasy/hope it doesn&#x27;t break type feeling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ergonomics is good though I do have to press the small button a couple of times to turn it on, only because that button is too dang small to fit my fingertip into.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Why do I take off 1-star?&lt;br /&gt;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&lt;br /&gt;Of all shavers, this one really, really needs a carrying case.  When I first opened it, I saw this small grey plastic thing on the bathroom floor.  Upon closer look it was the cleaning brush.  In the cardboard holder was the cleaning oil.  This can be easily lost.  In a perfect world, they&#x27;d incorporate a holder for the brush on the device itself like you would a stylus (and it&#x27;d be self-oiling ;) )&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then, to charge it, it&#x27;s not a simple, plug in this cord and lay it on the counter, it&#x27;s this large plastic contraption that grips the shaver at the sides to charge it.  I have little roomin my bathroom to begin with and none of my other shavers require such a large contraption - they just have a small plug.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then, the cleaning of it, which you&#x27;ll do every time you use it feels like I&#x27;m going to break it.  The plastic guard does not easily pop off, you just have to finagle with it and pull on the outer tabs or push them in until you wrestle the guard off to clean it (with the tiny cleaning brush you&#x27;ll have trouble finding again) and to oil it.  Add a one-click-pop-off button and I&#x27;d add half a star back.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Lastly, I kinda wish they&#x27;d cover the millimeter height marking when viewing the shaver from the back, because you may see 10mm, but on the *front* of the shaver that means 3mm or so.  If it&#x27;s 6am and you&#x27;re half awake, you could easily make the mistake the shaver is set to 10mm when it is really at 3mm.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall Summary:&lt;br /&gt;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&#x3D;&lt;br /&gt;My gripes are minor and livable.  This shaver still feels like higher quality and still far better than the Norelco BodyGroom and Panasonic ER224s.  Fix all the gripes and it will be an 5-star shaver, but for now, a solid 4-stars.</li>

    <li> REVIEW FOR SHAVER AS a \\&quot;BODY GROOMING\\&quot; DEVICE ONLY...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The funny thing is that even the Panasonic website doesn&#x27;t market this device as a \\&quot;body groomer\\&quot; but Amazon&#x27;s website does.  Regardless, I owned a Norelco goatee razor with a very similar design back in the mid-nineties.  I utilized it for \\&quot;dry\\&quot; body hair trimming and it worked quite well.  When I saw this had 19 different adjustments and could be used in the shower I was \\&quot;all in\\&quot;.  Upon receipt I observed that it is very lightweight, very modern, sleek and masculine looking.  This is never a bad thing in regards to a -- \\&quot;man groomer\\&quot; tool.  The long charging time (30 hours I believe) is a minor inconvenience.  If I were still single and needed a quick groom before regular dates with hotties this would be a significant downside of this razor.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ROUND 1:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On my first trial in the shower I tried shaving \\&quot;wet\\&quot; WITHOUT any liquid body wash.  That pointless experiment failed miserably.  The \\&quot;drag factor\\&quot; with the razor on skin was unbelievably terrible...the guard on the razor just kept bouncing across the skin but cut very little.  Thus, I immediately lathered up with body wash and began to shave away.  I went with the lowest setting and that achieved a nearly \\&quot;hairless look\\&quot;.  Someone would have to be \\&quot;up in your grill\\&quot; to see that body hair was present on your body.  Even with body wash applied I did have to hit some hairs from multiple angles.  I didn&#x27;t time it but I know I spent approximately 35-40 minutes in there to complete a FULL BODY SHAVE.  Even still some hairs were missed due to having to \\&quot;back track\\&quot; and try and hit hairs from multiple angles.  But overall it took care of 90% or so.  And possibly this will improve as my skill with it improves.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor didn&#x27;t seem extremely powerful but maybe that is because it is very quiet and doesn&#x27;t vibrate significantly.  I used to trim with an Oster hair clipper and you get quite a vibration with the pro models (plugged into the wall).  The clean-up with the Panasonic is easy as you simply hold it under a stream from your shower head.  The hair frees itself from the comb area pretty easily and washes down the drain.  This easy clean-up was the most compelling reason I was attracted to the idea of \\&quot;wet shaving\\&quot;.  When you \\&quot;dry shave\\&quot; with the Oster barber clippers hairs have a way of \\&quot;flying away from you\\&quot; and making a hand vacuum mandatory.  Contrary to my Oster barber clippers I didn&#x27;t have ingrown hairs running rampant post-shave with this Panasonic.  Contrary to other Amazon reviewers opinions I thought the razor disassembled for cleaning quite easily.  I did almost feel like I was going to break it given its lightweight materials and the way the guard pops off but it was no worse for the wear.  The map pointing to where you are to oil the razor isn&#x27;t perfectly diagrammed but you get the idea upon further examination.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, I think this is a very good product for BODY GROOMING with the only real recommendation being that a little more TORQUE to the motor may help cut those pesky hairs on the first go-around versus having to hit them from multiple angles.  My body hairs aren&#x27;t extremely coarse (like my facial hair) and it seems like I shouldn&#x27;t have so many problematic hairs.  However, since this same problem occurs with electric facial razors it is possibly just part of the reality of shaving and the way your hairs decide to grow in different directions.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ROUND 2:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The body groom on the lowest setting lasted about 2 weeks.  I think this is pretty standard for body shaving.  You go 3 weeks and it is just too hairy and doesn&#x27;t look good.  On this second attempt I used Dove Body Wash on a section of my body at a time (i.e. chest, left arm, right arm, left leg, right leg etc.) since soap dries quickly when you aren&#x27;t under the water.  This worked fairly well but I believe the ergonomics issue design of the shaver plus the human body (ex. difficultto shave lower leg due to bone or knee due to thin skin surrounding it etc.) it was not \\&quot;easy as pie\\&quot; to get the job done.  On Round 2 I spent about 45 minutes in the shower and had to hit some areas twice and had to hit the hair from ALL DIFFERENT ANGLES to shave it off.  By the end you really do just want it OVER as 45 minutes under the water makes you feel like a water mammal. Again, my hair isn&#x27;t very coarse and I am a moderately hairy dude.  NOTE: I did NOT shave the \\&quot;goose neck\\&quot; nor the \\&quot;eggs\\&quot;.  I don&#x27;t believe this type of shaver is ideal for that but if you raise the guard high enough you&#x27;re likely fine if you can pull the skin tawt.  At the end of the day, I think 80-85% of the hair was \\&quot;gonzo\\&quot; but this left me doing a brief touch-up dry shave with this razor outside of the shower.  I really do believe that it is either a WET SHAVE ELECTRIC issue OR a WEAK ASS MOTOR issue.  This razor is the softest, quietest I&#x27;ve ever heard and it clearly does chop hair but if the manufacturer gave it MORE TORQUE I think I could finish shaving quicker and easier.  I imagine someone with very coarse thick hair may have more issues than I&#x27;ve had given the not-so-powerful motor on this unit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My new rating for this shaver is:  *** 1/2&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Depending on how long the lifespan is on this and future results I may consider a Norelco Body Groomer on my next go-around.  We&#x27;ll see...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;ROUND 3:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I spent OVER 45 minutes in the shower doing \\&quot;body grooming\\&quot; (no goose neck or eggs) and even with MANY passes in all different directions I would say 25% of the hairs were missed.  I used a \\&quot;gel\\&quot; type body soap and a Dove \\&quot;creamy\\&quot; type body wash.  Neither worked much better than the other.  As a result, I had to do dry shaving outside of the shower and even that didn&#x27;t go smoothly (so-to-speak).  I spent another 30 minutes cleaning up all the MISSED HAIRS and still ended up with 10 % of the hairs being missed.  It&#x27;s an amount which will likely only by noticed by your female friend but given how much time I spent I expected better results.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The KEY PROBLEMS with this shaver APPEAR to be as follows:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;a)  The MOTOR is a weak pile&lt;br /&gt;b)  The BLADE isn&#x27;t sharp and thus barely cuts hairs and misses many so you have to hit them 12 times in all different directions&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As a result, my FINAL RATING &#x3D; ** 1/2 stars.</li>

    <li> I have owned several Panasonic trimmers and shavers. They are the best in the industry in my opinion, and this is due to several reasons: fast and relatively silent electric motor, capability of using them in both dry and wet mode, close shave, nicely engineered head and good to excellent overall quality.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This trimmer is no exception to all these features.     <li> [[VIDEOID:mo3OBC1WMIKYTZ7]]The ergonomics of the Panasonic Milano Men&#x27;s All-in-one Hair and Beard Trimmer are not the best.  The trimmer is light which is good for convenience but to the point of being so lightweight that it felt cheap and plastic.  The trimmer is not well balanced and this coupled with the lightweight feel led to the feeling that it is more of a toy than a serious trimmer. The power button is located on the bottom which means that it is awkward to turn on the trimmer from the same position as you would hold it while using it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer blades must be oiled after each use and a small container of oil is included.  A drop of oil must be applied in three spots.  A diagram is included on the trimmer body so that you know where to apply the oil even if you misplace the owner&#x27;s manual.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer has an integrated comb rather than removable combs.  The height of the integrated comb can be adjusted between 1mm and 10mm.  If you want hair at a length longer than 10mm you are out of luck with this trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As far as the trimming is concerned, the Panasonic trimmer works well and I had no problem using it.  The combs do have a little give, but not a significant amount and the combs remain in place even if you apply a bit of force while pressing the trimmers against your face.  Panasonic has done the comb design much better than some other brands.  I only wish that you could extend the height beyond 10mm.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A summary of some of the pros and cons of the Panasonic Milano Men&#x27;s All-in-one Hair and Beard Trimmer as discussed in the video are:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;- Can be used in the shower or under other wet conditions&lt;br /&gt;- Rather than to use combs to adjust the height of the trim, the trimmer has an integrated comb, the height of which is controlled with a dial on the side of the clippers&lt;br /&gt;- The comb can easily be removed to allow for the blades to be cleaned or to allow for fine trimming, for example squaringside burns.&lt;br /&gt;- Lightweight, but bordering on feeling too light&lt;br /&gt;- Quieter than other trimmers that I have used&lt;br /&gt;- Comb height does not change even when you press the trimmer against your face&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons&lt;br /&gt;- The maximum height of the comb is 10mm.  If you like your facial hair to be longer than that the clippers will not work for you.&lt;br /&gt;- The blades must be oiled before each use&lt;br /&gt;- The on / off button is inconveniently located&lt;br /&gt;- Long charge times&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I would recommend the Panasonic Milano Men&#x27;s All-in-one Hair and Beard Trimmer only to people who want to take advantage of the ability to use the trimmer in a wet environment.  Otherwise, I would recommend a clipper like the Remington Titanium Precision Pro instead because it offers greater flexibility for different lengths of hair.  The Remington comes with a collection of combs which allows for a much greater range of cutting heights, has better ergonomics and does not require oiling after each use.</li>

    <li> This is a really good rechargeable beard trimmer intended for regularly maintained beard or facial hair.  The cutting dial allows for highly precise length adjustments, from 1mm to 10mm, in half millimeter intervals along the way.  So if you&#x27;re really particular about the exact length of your beard, then this one should give all the control anyone needs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The charging base is nice - just place the shaver into it and a red LED lights up letting you know it&#x27;s charging (FYI - the red LED does Not go out once fully charged, it just stays illuminated the whole time the shaver is in the base.)  The base is a perfect cradle for this shaver; it doesn&#x27;t needlessly cling to the shaver, so it can easily be removed and placed back with one hand.  The metallic blue shaft and silver accent gives the shaver a chic look.  And most importantly, it does cut quite well and is relatively silent.  I did notice the blades don&#x27;t have quite the same, rock steady cutting power of a plugged in shaver, but that&#x27;s to be expected with most rechargeable battery shavers.  But for regular use, it&#x27;s a fair trade off to not have a cord dangling in my way.  This will probably be my go-to shaver for regular maintenance.  But if I ever decide to mow down to a goatee, or let my beard get a bit too long between touch-ups, then I&#x27;d probably reach for the full cutting power of my plug-in Wahl, since it can mow through anything with relative ease.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m not sure the wet/dry feature of this shaver is very meaningful; those are best for a clean shave and easy cleanup.  But for facial hair maintenance, the wet/dry thing is pretty much a meaningless gimmick; you&#x27;ll pluck as many hairs as you trim if trying to touch-up a wet beard, and rinsing longer stubble off the blades wont be as effective as just brushing them off.  (Yes, a small brush is included.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom Line - this is a really good beard trimmer that feels nice in the hand, and offers excellent precision and cutting ability for regularly maintained beards.for regularly maintained beards.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve only used it a couple of times, but it is so far the best facial trimmer I&#x27;ve ever used.  I&#x27;ve used Norelco in the past, and they were pretty decent, but I had to make several passes over my beard to get all the hair even.  With the Panasonic Milano ER-GB40-S, it takes two passes at the most.  You just have to make sure you go against the grain, especially my beard hairs go in all different directions.  From what I can see, there are two things this beard trimmer has over the competition.  First, the adjustable comb that has 19 length settings.  Sure, other facial trimmers have adjustable combs, but they&#x27;re often flimsy and interfere with the hair making contact with the blades.  Second, there&#x27;s a small groove in the comb in which the hair is not obstructed by the blade.  This simple addition is mind-blowingly effective in making sure that the comb keeps the hair at the selected level without interfering with it&#x27;s contact with the blades.  The only CON is that you have to take apart the blade assembly to clean and oil it.  And, according to the manual/instructions, you&#x27;re supposed to do this after you use it each time.  Despite that, I&#x27;m a life-long Panasonic facial trimmer user now.  I can confidently state that I will always own this trimmer or the closest version Panasonic has to offer well into the future, because my beard has never looked this good before with so little effort.</li>
